Shen Surname Murder Case: Higher Court Orders Autopsy Re-examination: The sensational murder case outside the West Gate of this county, which shocked Su and Chang, has been inspected twice by the county government. Both inspections concluded that the deceased, Shen Fugeng, only had minor injuries that were not fatal. However, the deceased's family insisted that he was beaten to death by Wang Erguan. Therefore, the county government specifically requested the Higher Court to order an autopsy re-examination. It is now learned that the Higher Court has sent an order to the county, stating that to avoid the trouble of travel, no one would be sent to Changshu. Instead, a doctor should be appointed within the original county to perform the autopsy and report the verified findings. After receiving the order, County Magistrate Tan summoned official doctors Shao Yufan, Xie Tang, and Huang Chengxi to the county government for discussion. All three doctors believed that the case had already been examined twice and determined to be minor injuries (Note: Xie and Huang were also involved in the first two inspections). Therefore, an autopsy would not make much difference. Moreover, whether the deceased's family was willing to undergo an autopsy was another issue. Even if it were approved, and the result still showed minor injuries, who would be responsible? Furthermore, the body had been buried for a long time and was already decomposed, making it even more difficult to detect injuries. Due to these various issues, the discussion ended without a result. It is now learned that the county government has scheduled to summon the Shen family and submit the opinions of the two official doctors to the Higher Court for review on the afternoon of the 22nd.

Wuxi

Gunfight Between Soldiers and Bandits on Train: Train No. 6, heading from Beijing to Wuxi, was passing Qixia Mountain near Zhenjiang at around 5:00 PM yesterday when Zhang Hong, a railway police inspector on board, was checking passengers in the third-class carriage. He noticed a suspicious-looking individual and proceeded to inspect him. He found a pistol on the person. Realizing that he had been exposed, the bandit violently attacked Zhang Hong, attempting to seize the pistol. At that moment, military police on board arrived and immediately apprehended him. Just as they were about to take him away for legal processing, nine other bandits emerged from the carriage to resist. A gunfight ensued inside the carriage, lasting about ten minutes. As a result, one bandit was killed, and Chen Shikui, Zhang Er, and Lou Kailuan were captured. Two Browning pistols were seized. The rest escaped by jumping out of the windows. The captured bandits were immediately escorted to Wuxi and handed over to the regimental headquarters for strict legal processing.

Water Chestnut Boat Robbed in Wuxi: Dai Youzhi, a native of Xinghua, has been selling water chestnuts in Qishuyan Town, which belongs to Changzhou County. Recently, Dai's goods were about to be sold out, and he planned to go to Hangzhou to purchase more. So, the day before yesterday, he took 300 yuan in capital and hired a boat, accompanied by a boatman, and set sail from the town. When passing through Lao Liku near Shitangwan in this county, it was late, so they stopped the boat and stayed overnight. Around midnight, a hooded boat suddenly approached, and four bandits jumped onto Dai's boat. They tied up Dai Youzhi and the boatman with ropes and stuffed cotton into their mouths. Then, they turned the rudder and searched the boat at will. After about an hour, they took the stolen goods, jumped back onto their original boat, and sped away. Dai and the boatman, seeing that the bandits were far away, checked their losses and found that the 300 yuan in capital they had brought was all stolen.

Public Security Bureau Busts Opium Den: Xu Jigui, the director of the Public Security Bureau of this county, received a tip-off yesterday morning (the 22nd) that a resident named Yang was privately selling opium and opium-smoking paraphernalia at his home in Xihetou in the city. He was making a lot of money and had never been caught in decades. Director Xu immediately secretly ordered Inspector Lei Jiaqu to dispatch several inspectors and police officers to search the premises. They caught the opium den owner, He Da (who was Yang's chauffeur), and eight opium smokers: Yang Jihua, Chen Liuxian, Qian Rongpei, Yang Dabao, Cao Zhongying, Hua Ruifu, and Yang Zhao. They also found a large number of opium lamps, pipes, and other evidence. They were all taken to the bureau. After Zhang, the section chief, held a trial, he prepared a document and presented it to the county court at 4:00 PM for a hearing and judgment.

Chamber of Commerce Meeting on Business Tax: The Wuxi County Chamber of Commerce held an emergency meeting of representatives from various industries yesterday to discuss how to comply with the provincial order to levy business tax starting on April 1st. More than 50 people from 35 industries attended. Qian Sunqing chaired the meeting. The meeting's proceedings were as follows: (1) The chairman reported on the meetings held in the town on April 3rd and 15th, as well as the petition process in the provincial and central governments. He stated that the provincial order had set April 1st as the starting date for levying the tax, and each industry should prepare in advance to avoid temporary disputes. The industry representatives believed that the business tax law had just been proposed and drafted by the Legislative Yuan, and the chambers of commerce in various counties were also requesting a reduction in the tax rate. If the tax were levied suddenly, the merchants and civilians would not know what to do. It was resolved that each industry association would submit a petition to the provincial government, requesting a postponement of the tax collection until the business tax law had been established by the Legislative Yuan. (2) The chairman reported on the meeting with the director of the business tax bureau and advocated for each industry to contract for tax payment to avoid various disputes. It was resolved that each industry association would hold separate meetings to discuss the plan and then reconvene to discuss the matter further. (3) Representatives of the soy sauce and wine industry stated that taxes such as public sales licenses had already been paid for alcohol, so how should this be deducted? It was resolved that alcohol should be removed, and only the income from the soy sauce and oil business should be reported. (4) Representatives of the timber industry said that the timber business was buying and selling on behalf of customers and had paid tooth tax (brokerage tax), so they should not have to pay business tax. It was resolved that the Chamber would send a telegram to the provincial government to clarify.

Case of the "Dexin" Steamboat Robbery Solved: On January 17th of last year, at around 8:00 AM, the "Dexin" small steamboat of the Yangxian Steamboat Company's Wuxi-Shu route was sailing from Wuxi to Shu. When passing through the Tanghe River near Gaoqiao in the 16th district, more than ten bandits suddenly fired at the steamboat from the shore. Three bandits, disguised as passengers, had already purchased tickets and boarded the boat. At this time, they also fired guns and forced the boat to stop. The passengers were robbed, and no one was spared, with losses amounting to over 3,000 yuan. After the incident, the company reported it to the county government for strict investigation. A secret informant recently tipped off County Magistrate Pan that the bandits, including Shi Jinyuan, were hiding in Shanghai. He immediately dispatched Wang Jinbiao, a special agent from the Water Patrol Team, to Shanghai with a warrant to investigate. Wang discovered that Shi Jinyuan was hiding in a thatched shed in Xiaoshadu Yaoshui Lane. He then worked with the chief of the 6th district police station to arrest Shi at his address and hand him over to the police station. After interrogation, Shi confessed that he was a 32-year-old man from Baoying. He was ordered to be detained. Yesterday, Qian Tianxiong, the captain of the Wuxi Water Patrol Team, went to Shanghai to escort Shi back to Wuxi for interrogation and legal processing.

Changzhou

Ministry of Railways Approves Reduced Freight Rates for Silk Cocoon Transport: The freight rate for transporting dry silk cocoons from Changzhou to Shanghai has always been higher than that from Wuxi. As a result, in recent years, many people have switched to transporting cocoons by boat. Last year, the Beijing-Shanghai Railway held a business meeting, and the Chamber of Commerce, based on the request of the Silk Cocoon Industry Association, proposed reducing the freight rate for dry cocoons. This was approved and submitted to the Ministry of Railways for review. The Chamber of Commerce submitted a report to the Ministry of Railways detailing how the high freight rates for cocoon transport were affecting railway revenue. The Ministry of Railways has now approved a 50% reduction in the freight rate for dry cocoons transported from Changzhou to the North Shanghai Station. After receiving this notice, the Chamber of Commerce forwarded it to the Silk Cocoon Industry Association for their information on the 20th.

Education News

Special Article

Reaffirming the Significance of the Child-Centered Approach

— Zheng Zonghai

The shift from a curriculum-centered approach to a child-centered approach in education represents a significant revolution, embodying the core of educational thought since Rousseau.

Rousseau was the first to raise the banner of revolution. He urged us to value children, stating, "You believe you know the value of time and fear wasting it, but you have not considered that if it is used improperly, it is better to let it pass. A child who is not taught properly is further away from goodness and beauty than someone who has not learned anything. You fear seeing him waste his childhood years, but is it really a waste to be happy and energetic, running and jumping all day? He will never be this happy again in his life. If someone refuses to sleep, believing that they would waste a part of their life otherwise, what would you think of this person?"

In the nineteenth century, Pestalozzi, Froebel, and others further promoted this idea. Researchers in child psychology have also provided us with a wealth of materials, enabling us to better understand the phenomena of children at various stages. The improvements in the content of elementary education in the past century can be attributed to this concept. Therefore, Adams said that the greatest contribution of modern educational theory is the discovery of the child, and using the child as the center of education.

This concept influences our view of education, especially educational methods. With the curriculum as the center, education is an external imposition, prone to standardization. With the child as the center, education is development, with less emphasis on conservatism and more on progress. All concepts such as "autonomy," "interest," and "individual adaptation" stem from this.

However, a person cannot exist independently from the environment. Our adaptation cannot always be purely self-centered. Moreover, to adapt appropriately, we must adopt or refer to the established methods of the current society. Therefore, the curriculum must be considered. The so-called "child-centered" approach does not ignore the curriculum, and completely separating from the curriculum would cause the meaning of development to lose its basis. Therefore, the child-centered approach is merely a matter of emphasis (see my translation of Dewey's original work, "The Child and the Curriculum," published by the Zhonghua Book Company). Furthermore, "child-centered" does not mean permissiveness, let alone indulgence. Educators should have a broad vision. However, adults, especially parents, must be careful not to "force growth" and must prevent "haste makes waste." On the one hand, they should base their actions on the needs and inherent energy of childhood, enrich their lives to develop their talents. Raggs said that "child-centered schools" should focus on two things: understanding the environment and expressing oneself. Dewey said, "Development lies in enabling children to have a deep understanding of a few representative situations, so as to gradually know how to deal with the problems of experience, rather than in the accumulation of knowledge." In this way, the gradual extension of attention, the accuracy of observation, and the methodical practice of memory and thought, especially the maintenance and development of the interest in seeking knowledge, are very important. Last year, Dewey said in the New Republic magazine that if new education does not emphasize the development of the intellectual aspects, then new education will be a failure.

Therefore, child-centered education not only wants children to be happy in their lives but also seeks to achieve the effects of children's lives. Of course, the happiness of children's lives cannot be ignored. Thorndike said, "In fact, if we get rid of adult tendencies, but seek adult benefits and convenience, and think about giving children innocent and carefree happiness, how cost-effective it is. Considering that children's likes and dislikes are often (but not always) a guide to their future happiness, and are no less reliable than our arbitrary decisions, then we should not regard current happiness as a trivial matter in school education." He meant that Dewey's education is an element of life, and wants "people to live happily and beneficially at every moment from birth to death." This "is not a doting attitude towards children, but purely a calm observation, knowing that this is the best way to achieve various highest and distant goals in life."

Article 13 of the internal policies of the platform of the Chinese Kuomintang states, "To fully develop child-centered education." Those engaged in elementary education must have a deep understanding of this and promote this meaning to families as well.

Important News

Regulations for Screening and Testing Graduates and Students of Unregistered and Closed Private Junior Colleges and Above

The Ministry of Education stipulates the qualifications and procedures for candidates

The Ministry of Education announced yesterday the regulations for screening and testing graduates and students of unregistered and closed private junior colleges and above. Article 1 states that graduates and students of unregistered and closed private junior colleges and above who possess one of the following qualifications at the time of enrollment may apply for screening and testing in accordance with these regulations: 1. Graduates of senior high schools; 2. Graduates of vocational schools equivalent to senior high school vocational courses; 3. Graduates of the old system middle school or senior high school who have studied for one year and entered the pre-university course for two years; 4. Graduates of the old system middle school or equivalent schools who have served for two years. Article 2 states that after applying, candidates must undergo qualification review. Those who do not meet the qualifications will not be allowed to take the test. Article 3 states that the qualification review will be conducted by the Qualification Review Committee organized by the provincial and municipal education departments at the test location. Article 4 states that the screening and testing will be conducted by the Screening and Testing Committee organized by the provincial and municipal education departments at the test location. The regulations will be specified separately. Article 5 states that the test is divided into two categories: basic subjects and specialized subjects. The basic subjects are Party Ideology, Chinese Language, Foreign Language, Social Sciences (choose one), and Natural Sciences (choose one). The specialized subjects will be determined by the Testing Committee based on the level of each grade in junior colleges and above. Each subject will be announced seven days before the test. Article 6 states that the evaluation of candidates' scores will be based on the test, with reference to qualifications and separate evaluations. If there is service experience, it may also be included and considered appropriately. Article 7 states that the results of the screening and testing will be reported by the Testing Committee to the Ministry of Education. Graduates with superior scores may transfer to the last grade of public or registered private junior colleges and above during enrollment (this is the result of the screening and testing, and the Ministry of Education will order public and registered private junior colleges and above to consider accommodating them and may not be restricted by Article 4 of the University Regulations and Article 4 of the revised Junior College Regulations). The remaining graduates and students will transfer to the corresponding grade based on their level. Article 8 states that candidates with extremely poor test scores and shallow academic qualifications who are unable to transfer to junior colleges and above may transfer to the corresponding grade of senior high school. Article 9 states that candidates will be issued a transfer certificate by the Ministry of Education upon completion of the test. The certificate is only valid for transfer and may not be used to prove other qualifications. Article 10 states that when applying, candidates must submit the following documents and fees: 1. Resume, high school graduation certificate, junior college or above graduation certificate or study certificate (if there is a service certificate, submit it together); 2. Two recent 4-inch half-body photos; 3. Test fee of one yuan. Article 11 states that the application date will be determined by the education departments of each province and city, but the deadline is June 10. The application locations are: Beijing - Beijing Municipal Education Bureau; Shanghai - Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau; Guangzhou - Guangdong Provincial Education Department; Wuchang - Hubei Provincial Education Department. Article 12 states that the test locations are in Shanghai, Beijing, Guangzhou, and Wuchang. The test venues will be determined temporarily by the Testing Committee in each location. The test date is scheduled to begin on June 26, held simultaneously in all four locations. Article 13 states that these regulations will be announced and implemented by the Ministry of Education and will be repealed upon completion of the test.

Ministry of Education Explains Doubts Regarding the Publication Law

The Ministry of Education has approved the Internal Affairs Ministry's response and explanation on various points of doubt regarding the Publication Law. It has instructed the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education, stating that, upon investigation, the department previously requested clarification on various points of doubt regarding the Publication Law. The Ministry relayed these requests to the Internal Affairs Ministry for interpretation and instructed the department to take note accordingly. Now, with the approval of the Internal Affairs Ministry's response, "the provincial government" as referred to in the Publication Law naturally refers to the provincial government as the competent executive authority. Publications distributed in counties and cities should also be submitted through the provincial government to which the city belongs to the Internal Affairs Ministry or directly to the Internal Affairs Ministry for handling in accordance with Articles 7 and 13 of the Publication Law. Counties and cities (cities not directly under the Executive Yuan) are not allowed to conduct registration of publications or review of books. However, if the county or city government discovers that publications distributed within its jurisdiction violate the restrictions of Articles 19 to 21 of the Publication Law, it may submit a request to the provincial government for legal action. The response is to be noted and the two counties, Yuyao and Jiaxing, are to be informed.

Zhejiang Province to

Discontinue Special Education Institutions Starting Next Semester

Various departments in Zhejiang Province run special education institutions to train specialized personnel for their needs. For example, the Finance Department runs a financial personnel training institute, the Construction Department runs construction personnel and weights and measures personnel training institutes, and the Civil Affairs Department runs an autonomous specialized school, police academy, police training institute, surveying personnel training institute, etc. The total annual expenditure is no less than over 400,000 yuan. Wang Chengying of the Finance Department, in view of the difficulty in matching the budget for the 20th year of the Republic, in addition to making substantial reductions in the new budget, believes that the current special talent in Zhejiang Province seems to be sufficient for application. After the existing students graduate, the recruitment of new students will be discontinued to bring these to a close.

Free Talk

A Word of Insight

— An Old Contributor

Love and money are the fuel of life. If the supply of fuel is cut off, the flame of life will be extinguished immediately.

Before marriage, the taste of love is intoxicating like mellow wine. After marriage, the taste of love is astringent and bitter like black tea.

The Young Master of the Garden said, "Girls are made of water, and men are made of mud." Therefore, when a man meets a woman, it is like a mud cow falling into water.

Unmarried women are truly like sacred and inviolable beings. Married women are just like that, nothing more. So-called great men are also like that.

The way to make friends is to be simple and tasteful. The same is true of love. The simpler, the more lasting and flavorful.

Only love for one's children can reduce love for one's husband. Therefore, there are more loving mothers than virtuous wives in the world.

Jealousy is the sublimation of a woman's love.

Love between the sexes is like the connection of opposite electrical currents. The power of the battery should be increased from time to time in order to maintain the spark of love.

A modern poem says, "A poor life with a simple hairpin is better than a flower." I hope that those in the world who have yellow-faced wives will be proud of this poem.

A Record of Xu Yousun, a Boatman on the West Lake

— Zhu Shoukuang

"Firmly plant your feet, the mountains behind you will not fly away; hold the handprint, the Buddha's face before you is as it is." This is a wonderful couplet in the newly built monastery of Yunlin Temple in West Lake. After my trip to Lingyin Temple, I walked to Yue Tomb and took a yacht back. The old boatman Xu Yousun said that he was fifty-eight years old, registered in Chongde, and had forty acres of land. Farming and eating was not a problem, and his two daughters were already married. One son could inherit his business, and he already had a grandson. Yousun comes to Hangzhou every year in February to work as a boatman, and then returns to his hometown in late August. He spends his years leisurely. The income from boating in Hangzhou, after deducting half a yuan for daily food and drink, still has a surplus, which is enough for his usual use. Therefore, he is carefree on the lake, very happy. I said, "You already have a small fortune, and you don't worry about food and clothing. When you are almost sixty years old, you still work at this. Isn't it hard?" Yousun smiled and said, "Sir, do you think I am working hard? I am enjoying it. The scenery of West Lake is the best in the world. From the south of Baiyue to the north of Yanji, wealthy merchants and officials spend huge sums of money every year to visit this land, but they only stay temporarily. But I don't spend a penny, and I am in the lake scenery day and night. With a light stroke of the oar, I can roam freely and contentedly. I work during the day and rest at night, and I am self-reliant. I don't ask for help and I don't worry about food. I am actually doing a job for leisure, not making a living for food. I have three things I don't do in this business: one is strong wind, two is rain and snow, and three is dawn on the first day of the lunar month, even if I am paid a heavy price. Because wind and rain are dangerous and hard work, I will definitely go to Tianzhu Temple to visit the Goddess of Mercy on the first day of the lunar month, no matter whether it is sunny or rainy. Mr. Ma Yinchu once sat in my boat and talked very happily. I don't know what economics is, but I know how to live within my means, not accumulating wealth and not wasting it. The world is just a temporary inn, and people must know how to be content. God has given me an old but not frail body, so I can enjoy what I enjoy. What more can I ask for? Last year, I had a surplus of funds, so I spent a hundred yuan to take care of my funeral affairs. Once I die, I will have a place to go. From then on, I will be free and unfettered, and the years of my life will be nothing but happy days." At this point, the boat had reached the shore. Yousun received the money and thanked me, and with a light stroke of the oar, he plunged back into the depths of the misty waves. I returned to my residence and remembered the couplet in the monastery and what the boatman said, and I couldn't help but feel lost for several days.

A Record of Sorting Out the Posthumous Manuscripts of Juemi

— Wu Kezhen

In the recent three or five years, my late brother Juemi devoted himself to reading books because he had been serving our late mother with illness and living in the countryside for a long time. In addition to serving medicine, he devoted himself to reading books. The reason for this is that my late grandfather and great-grandfather did not manage fields, and the income from official travel and the inkstone field was used to purchase books. Therefore, he continued his ancestors' aspirations. The books in the family are stored, although they are not enough to be called ten thousand volumes, but they have already occupied five rooms. Juemi sat in the book city every day, and he was happy and carefree, without worrying about loneliness. The daily progress of his writing and the increase in his writing were all due to the small study. The publications published in lead printing are countless, and he feels that he has gained research experience in textual research. Although my family has very few fine engraved isolated copies, the local chronicles of various provinces are indeed numerous. Now I have examined his posthumous manuscripts, and it seems that there are more than twenty kinds that are slightly valuable for writing. Due to my weak ability, none of them have been published. I will briefly describe one or two to inform you. Those about history include: A History of Shanghai Diplomacy, An Interpretation of the Yangjingbang Regulations, A History of the Evolution of Concessions in Various Places, A Study of the Origin of Dredging the Wusong River, and Miscellaneous Records of Border Defense in the Qing Dynasty, a total of six kinds. A manuscript of A History of Shanghai Diplomacy has now been handed over to Mr. Ye Mujiao of the Diplomatic Department for preservation. Those about textual research include: Corrections to the Chronology of Past Dynasties, Textual Research on Ancient Sites in the Yangtze River Basin, Detailed Textual Research on the Holy Sites of Qufu, and Jianghu Bai Opera. This book details the origins and responses of the Three Religions and Nine Schools since the Qin and Han Dynasties, and is linked to the biographies of various famous people. There are also Shanghai Ancient Tomb Archaeological Records, Small Records of the Sex of Various Collectors, and Miscellaneous Records of Ancient Inkstone Inscriptions, a total of seven kinds. Those about miscellaneous compilations include: Du's Poetry Notes on the Left Bank of the Huangpu River, two volumes. This book is the posthumous work of Du Yuesheng, a famous person in Shanghai. However, they are all scattered in various poetry collections or manuscripts. It took many years of effort to compile them. It has now been handed over to Mr. Yuesheng for preservation. There are also six volumes of selected notes and several kinds of expository book notes. The so-called expository book notes are diaries of the daily sorting of books stored at home, which are used as the basis for compiling a bibliography after completion. There are many other fragments. I plan to make some slight adjustments and choose the best ones for publication. Li Youzhi, the brother-in-law of a Shanghai Chinese scholar, has agreed to take on the task of compiling them, and will combine the remaining short articles and fragments and title them Juemi Series for publication. It is a pity to let Juemi's life's work be lost. As for the unorganized books in the family, I plan to process them systematically during the summer vacation. My friend Chen Zibao, former librarian of the Jiande Savings Association, has considerable experience in the preparation of bibliographies. Now he has agreed to my request to help me organize them and complete the expository book notes. Although I am unworthy, I will of course do my best to preserve the ancient books in the family. Otherwise, the legacy of my ancestors will be completely lost. If Juemi knows, he will have no regrets in the afterlife.

After Watching the Screening of "Human-Animal Spectacle"

— Yu Kaixu

A few days ago, I was invited by the deacons of the Carlton to attend the preview of "Human-Animal Spectacle" at the Grand Light Cinema. At first, I didn't know the content of the film, and I thought it was just a work of similar material to the previous hunting photography films. I have always regarded the previous films as ordinary. Later, I heard from someone who had read the book that there were quite a few disturbing things in the film. This film was made entirely based on the actual situation in Africa, and cannot be compared with those created by imagination. When the screen opened, I realized that the film was made jointly by the various colonial governments, great explorers, and great hunters in Africa. Otherwise, it would not have been possible to make this film so great and would have been reduced to child's play in an ordinary circus. Furthermore, the sacrifice made in this film was huge. In addition to the deaths and injuries of wild animals such as lions, rhinos, tigers, and leopards, the sacrifice of human life was the greatest. There were piles of human heads and half-rotten human corpses. It was not just for the filming of this film that cruel and inhumane actions were deliberately taken. They were all adventurously photographed from the cannibal countries of Africa. Other things, such as the hunting of lions and leopards, the fighting of groups of lions, etc., were also not fictitious. Watching it, in addition to shaking my bones and being unbearable, I could indeed know the real situation in the barren forests of Africa. As for the greatest sacrifice, it was that a black man was killed by a rhinoceros. The rhinoceros is the most ferocious of the beasts, and anyone who comes into contact with it will die immediately. Another huge lion was stabbed in the brain by a black man with a sharp stick that was about a foot long. The lion roared like thunder, jumped wildly three or four times, and then fell to the ground and died. In other cases, the cannibal countries of Africa hunt human heads in all directions, beating drums and shouting loudly. Just hearing the sound can make you tremble with fear. Furthermore, in the cannibal country, there is a female chief who is extremely beautiful. Her ancestors were probably white people who fell into the cannibal country. Later, she was rescued by white people. This is an insertion that the author cannot but make. Otherwise, this film will lose its spiritual regulation. As for me, as the reporter, I had a beautiful and unparalleled, graceful and natural, yellow-haired, slender-bodied wild woman in front of me, which made me unforgettable for a long time. After watching this film, I still feel that everything is vivid in my mind.

An Eulogy

— Tao Zaidong

At the beginning of every obituary, there must be an image. The image must have an eulogy. The eulogy must be brilliant and written by great figures of the time. In fact, it is still a few poor scholars who touch their beards and hold their pens, doing a poor job. The so-called bitter interest of the Tathagata, I have also tasted a share of this bitter interest. After a long time, I realized the mistakes I made. The mistake was that the text did not match the topic. If you examine the works, they are all biographies and eulogies, not image eulogies. Since it is named image eulogy, it is only suitable to praise the image. Therefore, a great revolution began in the image eulogy world, and the image eulogy of a new era is as follows:

Praise the head of the deceased, shaped like a bamboo basket, drilled like a awl tip. Praise the eyes of the deceased, like a sling, with a small capacity but shallow eyelids, and an improper chest but dull pupils. Praise the nose of the deceased, with two holes facing the sky, not knowing fragrance or stench, like pomace wine. Praise the mouth of the deceased, like a crosstalk actor shouting, able to open a basin of blood, but unable to wag a three-inch tongue. Cupping the beak, the pig is Bajie, and closing the mouth, the bird is Li Kui. Praise the ears of the deceased, not knowing a single secret, big and upright like the Rabbit God, small and twitched like a mouse. Are these distinctive five senses not worthy of careful examination? Originally, the image in ancient times was only made of stone. Now it is flexible, and the image is taken by a mirror. It can be enlarged or reduced. There are several life photos, and this set must come for the death obituary. It is enough to commemorate and to fulfill filial piety. Why do you write texts that do not match the topic and wear hats that do not fit the head? There are many tasteless compliments, which come with the ridicule of those who know. If the dead have knowledge, they will be frightened when they see it. Therefore, Xun Qing wrote "Discourses on the Appearance", and Tantai lost his appearance. Seven mouths and eight tongues, ten hemp and nine beauties. Dimples are charming and forehead is born, eyelashes are soft and cheeks are surrounded. When the monk gets angry, his appearance is ugly. When the emperor is chopped, his neck is good. The red-headed aesthetic A-San, the powdered double-material Cao Cao. What is there to be a land of spirits and heroes? It is simply born unfilial. Moreover, the head is like a deer, the eyes are like a mouse, the nose is like a hawk, and the eyes are like a falcon. The skin is beautiful and the bones are ugly, and the fat intestines are full of brains. The muscles do not bind the bones, which is called ghostly agitation. Intrinsic cowardice and stern expression, stealing through holes. The ears eat the memory and have light, the face is not needed but is often swept. There must be plague and insatiable greed. Making feces is a complete machine, and a mess is an inverted treasure. Four feet face the sky, and the braid must be raised. When a breath does not come, three people look at each other and laugh. Alas, how can it not be early?

Brief News: Ms. Ziluolan, a famous Cantonese singer and dancer, has returned to Shanghai to perform again, winning the praise of the audience. Ms. has also made a trip to Jin-Ping. Yesterday, I received a letter from my friend Li Ziyuanxing, who came from Ping, saying that the Nancheng Amusement Park in Beiping specially hired Ms. to perform on stage. Like a fairy scattering flowers, Bao Lian Deng, Wu Jia Po, Lou Dong Yuan, Half-sided Chicken, Babu Lao teaching his daughter, Picking Flower Girl, Xiao Qing Hanging Shadow, Chan Fang Night Resentment, Huo Xiaoyu, Suzhou Small Songs, Toe Dance, Ziluolan Dance, etc., all are wonderful and unparalleled. Therefore, the press has praised her greatly. (Rui Hongchu)

A True Account of the Execution of Taibao Ashu (Part 2)

— Zhutian

Ten Yuan for Outfit: This time, Wang Fusheng, the executioner hired in Shanghai, and his three assistants used to specialize in this profession during the Sun Chuanfang era. In recent years, with the abolition of beheading, Wang and others had fallen on hard times in Shanghai, struggling to make a living. They were overjoyed to be summoned this time, but because their clothes were tattered, they requested money for an outfit. Each was given ten yuan to buy a set of black lined clothes and trousers, get a haircut and bath, and appear brand new. In total, each person earned an average of twenty to thirty yuan this time, which was enough to cover their living expenses for more than a month.

Sent to His Children: From the time Taibao Ashu was escorted away until his execution, the one thing he couldn't stop thinking about was his two surviving sons. According to custom, the clothes worn by a condemned prisoner at the time of execution belonged to the executioner. However, at the time of the binding, Taibao Ashu's blue crepe cotton robe and a set of blue silk gauze lined jacket and trousers were still worth a considerable sum. Therefore, he instructed the soldiers to pawn the clothes and send the proceeds to his two sons as temporary relief. Those who heard this agreed. However, the address of the two sons was unknown, so there was no way to send it to them. Naturally, it still ended up in the executioner's pocket. If the dead have knowledge, they must be deeply grieved.

Claiming to Follow Orders: After Taibao Ashu and his brother arrived at the execution ground, the executioner Wang Fusheng and his assistants were already there. The knife they held was of the type used by the Big Sword Squad, with a newly sharpened blade that gleamed. Taibao Ashu and his brother knelt back-to-back. Taibao was executed first, followed by his brother. The whole process took less than three minutes. During the execution, one person held Taibao's hands behind his back and said, "Following orders, this has nothing to do with me." Another person held a rope around Taibao's neck, pulling it forward, also saying, "Following orders." Finally, the executioner approached and patted Taibao's abdomen, saying, "Following orders to kill you, please don't blame me." Then he lightly pressed on Taibao's neck, holding the knife behind his back in his right hand. At this point, the person holding Taibao's hands shouted loudly, and in an instant, the executioner raised his knife and brought it down, slashing several times. The head fell to the ground. At that time, although Taibao's brother witnessed his brother's death, his expression remained unchanged. It can be said to be the most tragic event imaginable.

Blood Money for Exorcism: According to custom, the shackles should be broken after the execution. The shackles of Taibao Ashu and his brother weighed about seven pounds. After the heads were severed, the executioner used the knife handle to break the shackles. However, Taibao's brother, Xu Fusheng, injured his foot accidentally during the breaking. Bloodstains were evident on the outside of his sock. After the execution, spectators each took out copper coins, suspended a short rope through the coin hole, and dipped the rope into the blood from the severed neck, saying it could suppress evil. They carefully wrapped it in white paper and put it in their pockets. Some women who had come from afar to watch even bought these evil-suppressing coins at the price of several yuan. Their foolishness was beyond compare.

Travelogue of India (32)

— Linghua

Indians have large bodies. The travel beds they sell are about eight inches longer than those in China, which proves it. Their hair is black, which is different from Europeans, but their deep-set eyes and high noses are different from Easterners, but similar to Europeans. However, their noses are not as sharp as those of Caucasians, which is proof that they are both Aryans. According to Indians, they originally came from the upper reaches of the Ganges River in the Pamir region and were originally called Brahmins. As for the indigenous people of India, they already existed. They are the most primitive people with the lowest level of culture. Some small groups are still preserved in the mountains and forests, it is said. This is probably the same as the Miao people in China and the Ezo people in Japan.

Most Indian men have their hair cut, but the most interesting thing in the lower classes is that they only leave a small portion on the top of their heads, a few dozen strands, like a child's braid in our country. Some women also cut their hair. The custom of piercing the nose remains, which is the most unaesthetic.

There is a kind of expression in Indian gestures that we easily misunderstand, which is their habit of shaking their heads. If we think that agreeing is nodding, and disagreeing is shaking, Indians are the opposite. Their shaking their heads indicates approval. I often misunderstood or could not understand. It was only after a long time that I gradually understood. But I'm still not used to it.

On the 17th, I happened to pass by a place and was very hungry and thirsty. I saw a snack shop and went in to eat. I sat and drank cold water. They gave me a clay cup to drink from. The snacks were delicious. After eating, they told me to take the rest of the snack with me, otherwise I had to throw it in the street. They also told me to throw the clay cup on the street and break it. I didn't understand very well and asked firmly. They confirmed that I should throw it, break it, and throw it away. I was very surprised. This is a strange custom. The cup is only allowed to be used once, and the snacks are not allowed to be left over. What is the reason? I remember that Japan has this custom. The way they use chopsticks is that they must use new ones for every meal. The chopsticks are made of poplar wood, which is very light and easy to break, like using toothpicks. But from my experience, it's only big hotels that show off. I often stay in small rental houses, and I see that the owners don't do that. Why is it that Indians' clay cups are only used to drink water once and not a second time? I asked a gentleman. He replied that this is Hinduism. It is for hygiene reasons. Cups used by the living cannot be used indiscriminately, so they are discarded. Food left over by the living cannot be eaten, so it is discarded. Due to different customs, there may be infectious diseases, so people dare not enter the homes of others lightly to eat and drink. I believe that these things are mostly suggested by religious people to reject other religions, which only increases social taboos and obstacles. If it is really for hygiene, I dare to say that it is not true. There are many taboos, and people dare not contact others, which is not suitable for today's world. I realized why the ethnic groups in Southeast Asian countries have not been able to assimilate for thousands of years, which is due to the taboos of each religion and ethnic group. Today, the world is becoming one, and there will inevitably be a day to sweep away and eliminate these things. How can these bad customs be allowed to exist? Entering a village, one must ask about the customs, which also makes us feel helpless. In short, Indian customs make us feel like we are lost in a fog, which is very difficult to understand.

Gold Market Soars

Big Players Frenziedly Buy, Weak Ones Anxious

Very Strong Buying Sentiment: Yesterday, the gold price rose fiercely and unstoppably on the 22nd. The situation was sharp, rushing forward. Bai Yuan (white yuan rice) arrivals and sales were evenly matched, and there was no advantage or disadvantage.

South Shanghai: Yesterday, over ten boats were seen arriving at the river. Sales on this street turned sluggish. Changshu and Suzhou japonica rice were still firm in the early morning but then turned flat. Towards the closing market, the outgoing path was increasingly stagnant, with signs of weakening. Southern guilds' Bo Zao (thin early) rice's top-grade goods were quite popular, while ordinary grades were unsatisfactory. The general trend was high and firm, while secondary grades were stable. Yang Du and other sharp-edged customers' guilds had weak appetites, and retail sales were also average, with little price fluctuation. Bian Yuan (varied yuan rice) turned yin (negative), showing a state of arriving little and selling slowly. Except for high-quality goods with active and flat prices, the rest were slightly reduced in price. The overall market's negative opening was only 9 yuan and 6-7 jiao.

Ke Xian (Guest Indica) Market Extremely Quiet

Yesterday's guest indica rice market was exceptionally quiet. Because the Guangdong guild stopped trading, other local guests had no appetite. There were still a few Jiangxi rice stocks. Apart from the company's own carload goods, the guest merchants mostly did not inquire. The remaining stocks of Jiangxi rice were not much, and the cargo owners were quite speculative. However, with few goods, it was difficult to choose, and the guest guilds watched, so the market price was ultimately difficult to rise. Throughout the day, only the Beiyang guild purchased over 50 packages of Jiangxi Zhongguanji rice, priced at 13 yuan. There were no other transactions. However, the local guests still had a good appetite for guest yuan rice, only disliking the low inventory and poor quality, unable to fully enjoy and purchase, it was said.

Wheat Futures Market Initially Flat, Then Weak

Yesterday's wheat futures market showed signs of initially being flat and then falling in the morning and afternoon sessions. The market in the current month initially opened well, followed by the fact that although some of the goods for delivery in the current month failed to meet the standards and were withdrawn, a few had already agreed to mutually deduct the standards. Therefore, the long side seemed unable to compete with the short side, so it fell again and again, dropping as much as 7 cents compared to the previous day's closing. The various far-term months were initially stable, but later, due to the clear weather and the hedging sales of traders, the market also showed signs of weakening. Observing the subsequent steps, it may still be flat and weak. As a result, the current month fell 7 cents compared to the previous day, May and June fell 5 cents, July fell 6 cents, August fell 5 cents, and September fell 3 cents, it was said.

Flour Futures Market Difficult to Escape Weakness

Yesterday's flour market showed a trend of initially weakening and then becoming buoyant after the opening of the morning session. Because foreign wheat was reported to be good, there were fluctuations of one or two jiao. The greater impulse was due to the sudden rain the previous day, and yesterday it cleared up. Some people inevitably changed due to the rain, so the opening was slightly lower by nearly a cent. Later, speculative longs became active again, so the near and far terms recovered and stabilized. When the afternoon session opened, the appetite of the Tianjin guild had not yet been activated, and the local spot flour was also slightly lower by one cent (3 yuan and 9 cents), so people were generally sluggish. Observing the subsequent steps, it is feared that the environment will become unfavorable again, and it is also unknown whether the far term will return to the 2 tael mark. As a result, the current month was down by 7.5 li compared to the previous day, May was down by 1 cent, and June to September were down by 1.25 li.

Soybean Futures Trended Soft in the Afternoon

Yesterday, the Dalian standard soybeans opened extremely well. The near and far term months were inquired by guest guilds and factories, so the current month once reached 4 taels and 7 qian. Currently, the exchange has traded a large amount of over a thousand carloads. Although they are transported from Dalian Wuzhuang, Yingkou, etc., because of the risk of substandard goods, people are extremely cautious. When the afternoon session opened, the telegraph from Dalian reported a decrease of 9 fen, so the market turned soft, and the price changed from firm to weak. As a result, the April term was 4 taels and 6 qian and 8 fen, and the June term was 4 taels and 6 qian and 6 fen, both down by 1 fen, while the May term was unchanged.

Local News

Central Bank Issues

Customs Gold Unit Exchange Certificates

Minister of Finance Song Ziwen Speaks

Issued on May 1st of this Year

Minister of Finance Song Ziwen spoke about the Central Bank's issuance of Customs Gold Unit exchange certificates yesterday as follows:

The bank, under government order, will issue Customs Gold Unit exchange certificates starting May 1st of this year. The issuance of these Customs Gold Unit exchange certificates is intended to facilitate the payment of customs duties by importers in Shanghai or other ports. Currently, importers pay customs duties by temporarily converting silver dollars to pay taxes, except for those who have Customs Gold Unit deposits in the Central Bank and can issue checks at any time to pay. From now on, they can directly pay with Customs Gold Unit exchange certificates or Customs Gold Unit checks, which is more convenient. It is even more convenient in ports where the Central Bank does not have branches. These Customs Gold Unit exchange certificates have full reserves. The types of reserves, cash on hand or foreign gold coins, should be at least 60% or more. The rest can be filled with bank acceptance drafts or gold bonds with good foreign credit. Upon exchange, the Central Bank will issue immediate bank drafts in foreign financial markets for exchange. However, when the Customs Gold Unit is less than 1,000 yuan, the Central Bank can exchange it for silver dollars at the market rate of the day. As for the amount of issuance and reserves, the bank will still follow the silver dollar exchange certificate method, and publish it in the newspaper after the audit by the board of supervisors every ten days to show credit. The current supervisors of the bank are Li Ming, Wang Jingli, Qin Runqing, Lin Kanghou, Ju Zuyi, Yu Qiaqing, and Xu Chenmian. Furthermore, the government has ordered that the right to issue these Customs Gold Unit exchange certificates belongs exclusively to the Central Bank, it was said.

Yesterday's Publicly Elected Office

Announced National Assembly Representatives

Electoral Groups: 80 Electoral Units, 48,987 Voters

Chen Guansheng, Hou Dachun, Wang Yansong, and Hu Shuhua Elected

The election of representatives to the National Assembly in this city ended yesterday. The staff mobilized by the publicly elected office has ceased to work at the office yesterday, leaving only a few people to conclude unfinished matters. The list of elected representatives was officially announced by the office yesterday. The details of each item are recorded below:

Number of Electors: The number of groups participating in the election this time includes: 7 agricultural associations, with 3,156 electors; 49 labor unions, with 34,179 electors; 1 commercial association, with 388 electors; 23 free professional groups, universities, and educational associations, with a total of 1,164 electors. The total number of groups is 80, with 48,987 electors.

Difficulties: The number of electors in this election was not strong, and the reasons are: (1) The labor union was just reorganized on March 15 and was in the process of sorting out its affairs and reporting the electoral registers, which was not enough time. Therefore, it was not a small number of those who reported only a part. (2) There were no organizations for agricultural and educational associations in this city until the end of this month, when several places were established. (3) Among the free professional groups, some gave up on their own, and some were unable to participate in the election because the organization was not prepared. (4) The number of electors represented by the commercial association should be more than 45,000, but the electors represented are only the representatives of the trade and shop guilds attending the commercial association. If the agricultural, educational, and labor unions had been reorganized and completed earlier, the number of electors in this city would have been at least 230,000.

Elected Representatives: Chen Guansheng of the Agricultural Association, with 1,796 votes, the next largest number of votes was Chen Tianxi with 19 votes; Hou Dachun of the Labor Union, with 14,442 votes, the next largest number of votes was Wang Zhuping with 1,426 votes; Wang Yansong of the Commercial Association, with 169 votes, the next largest number of votes was Xu Jimiao with 3 votes; Hu Shuhua of the Free Professional Groups, Universities, and Educational Associations, with 2,653 votes, the next largest number of votes was Zheng Yuxiu with 336 votes.

Notification of Election: The election office in this city, in addition to publishing the names of the elected representatives with the most votes in the newspaper, and sending a telegram to the general office, also notified the elected representatives, it was said.

Follow-up Report on the

Huayang Run Aground

Hope of Saving the Hull Seems Lost

Crew and Passengers Safe Uphill

Loaded onto Chengli Wheel to Shanghai Today

The Hang'an Company's Huayang steamship encountered fog and ran aground on the Haishan Island in Wenzhou. The report was already published yesterday. Regarding the rescue situation of the steamship, our reporter conducted a thorough investigation from all aspects. After the accident, all the crew and passengers escaped to the reef mountain by small sampans, so they were safe and sound. However, the hull was damaged by the reef and could not be towed for rescue. The details are recorded as follows:

True Picture of the Accident: This time, the Huayang steamship left Shanghai on the afternoon of the 20th and set sail for Xinghua. On the afternoon of the 21st, at 2:30 pm, when it was traveling to the vicinity of Nan Yushan reef, 90 nautical miles from Haishan Island, Wenzhou, the steamship encountered heavy fog. The owner of the ship, W. Sokoloff, a Russian, intended to anchor and take temporary shelter, but it was too late. The hull immediately hit the mountain reef. Although the extent of the damage was not mentioned in the telegram, it seems that the bottom of the ship has been set into the reef and seawater rushed into the various cabins, the situation is very critical. The time of the accident was 2:30 pm.

Foreign Ships First Rescued: The first distress telegram sent by the owner of the ship was received by the Tientien Beienke steamship of Tianshang Foreign Firm. Then the Gongping Wheel received it. At 4:35 pm on the 21st, the Tianshang Wheel first opened to Haishan Island to carry out the rescue. However, the fog was too great to advance, so the steamship sent a telegram to Shanghai, briefly stating that Huayang was 90 miles away from Haishan Island, and we had come to rescue, but the fog was very heavy, etc. At 5:30 pm, Gongping also arrived, but because the draft was too deep, it was impossible to get close, and the fog also covered the sea, making it difficult to release the sampan. It was helpless to look at the sea and sigh.

Passengers Aboard the Mountain: After the Huayang steamship ran aground, there were about 130 crew members and passengers. The ship owner and the comprador Yue Yaosheng, etc., took life jackets and released the sampan boats, first carrying the passengers on board to Nan Yu reef in batches for temporary refuge. According to reports, on the afternoon of the 21st, all the ship's staff and passengers had safely ascended the mountain without anyone being injured. It was also a great fortune in misfortune.

Degree of Grounding: Yesterday, the Hang'an Company also received a telegram from the English steamship stating that the Huayang accident site was designated by the 300th in the navigation warning table, the grounding site was at 18 degrees north latitude and 6 degrees west longitude. At 2:35 pm, another telegram was received from the Gongping, saying that the Huayang steamship was grounded, the place name was Nan Yu Mountain, close to Haishan Island, and there was no way to rescue it. Gongping was short of water and planned to find another solution.

British Ships Assist: The British Company's mail ship, Laganpura, was exported from Shanghai to England and heard the news of the Huayang accident while passing through the waters of Wenzhou, so it also sailed to Ma'an Island to help rescue. It arrived at Haishan Island at 11:00 am yesterday, first flying a flag to ask the Gongping Wheel, and the Gongping shipowner replied that all the Huayang crew members and passengers had been rescued to Nan Yu Mountain, and the company had sent another ship to rescue.

Two Ships to the Rescue: Yesterday morning, because Hang'an Company received a telegram from Gongping stating that the steamship lacked food and drinking water and could not rescue, it asked the local Shunan Wheel Company to send a telegram to the Fusheng Wheel on the same route to sail to the rescue. At that time, the Fusheng Wheel had returned from Xinghua and had arrived at Wusong, without entering the port, it immediately turned back to Nan Yu Mountain. At the same time, it negotiated with the Zhengji Company, asking it to telegram the Chengli Wheel, which was currently in Wenzhou, to sail nearby to help the rescue. After the two ships were dispatched, at 2:53 pm, another telegram was received from the Gongping, saying that this steamship could not stay for a long time due to lack of furnace water. The British mail ship had arrived at the scene of the Huayang accident and was anchored to protect it. The Chengli Wheel will arrive at 3:00 pm, and the passengers and crew members on the mountain will be rescued by the Chengli Wheel's sampan boat and taken back to Shanghai.

Dispatch a Warship to Protect: After Jianghai Customs was notified by the coastal radio station, it dispatched the Liujing warship yesterday morning to protect the area. The manager of Hang'an, Huang Xingge, in order to protect the passengers, goods, and prevent pirates from looting, especially went to the Naval Headquarters to request the dispatch of a warship to protect the area. The naval authorities have agreed to send a telegram to the Yongjian warship stationed in Ningbo to sail nearby to protect the stranded steamship.

Ship and Cargo Losses: The Huayang Wheel was originally owned by Wang Jiaojang. This year, it was purchased by Hang'an Company for 100,000 yuan. First, it was sent to the northern seas of Yantai, Tianjin, and Yingkou. Recently, it was transferred to Shanghai and Xinghua. It was only the third time it had sailed after being purchased. The steamship had a deadweight of 1,600 tons, and the hull was insured by the bureau itself. The export goods loaded in Shanghai this time included 1,200 tons of soybeans, soybean cakes, piece goods, raw oil, kerosene, and groceries. It is heard that the hull has been destroyed and there is no hope of saving it. It will be abandoned. According to the person in charge of the company, the first priority is to rescue the crew members and passengers, and the second is to unload the goods in order to protect the capital of the merchants. The crew members' luggage and passengers' belongings, etc., were not able to be taken out and were completely sacrificed. Therefore, although the Huayang accident did not harm any lives, the public and private losses were very huge. As for the victims, it is expected that they will be rescued back to Shanghai today.

Trade Associations' Declaration

Support the Central Government's Implementation of the Business Tax Plan

Must be Equal Between Chinese and Foreign, and Chinese Rentals Uniform

The local North-South Goods Dismantling and Exchange Industry, Wood Industry, Native Cloth Industry, Fruit and Local Goods Industry, Kerosene Industry, Ice-Fresh Fish Industry, North Goods Industry, Western Clothing Industry, Local Goods Industry, Pawnshop Industry, Money Industry, Department Store Industry, Rice Shop Industry, Soybean and Rice Industry, Gold Industry, Paint Industry, Woolen Fabric Factory Industry, South Goods Industry, Tea Industry, Duck Slaughtering Industry, Knitting Industry, Seafood Grocery Industry, Firewood and Coal Industry, Egg Industry, Chinese Medicine Industry, New Medicine Industry, Chinese Soap Industry, Chinese Candle Industry, Chinese Grain and Oil Cake Industry, Cotton Cloth Industry, Shoe, Leather, Nail and Shoe Tree Industry, Sausage Industry, Tobacco Leaf Industry, Tobacco Exchange Industry, Electrical Machinery and Silk Factory Industry, Coal Industry, Fur Industry, Jewelry Industry, Ginseng and Bird's Nest Industry, Sauce Garden Industry, Securities Industry, Medicinal Materials Industry, Foil Industry, Ham Industry, Silk and Satin Industry, Insurance Industry, etc., 180 trade associations, issued an announcement yesterday regarding the matter of supporting the central government's promotion of business tax negotiations, saying: "Stealing the principle of tax law, the first lies in equality. All those who operate the same business in the same region should bear the same tax rate. It is the law of nature and what should be done. Therefore, the prerequisite issues for organizing business tax in this city are (1) equality between Chinese and foreigners, and (2) uniform Chinese rentals, so as to avoid the disadvantages of uneven light and heavy taxation, and not to make concessions and nominally foreign shops, serve as the act of crows gathering and scaring sparrows. Now, on the 16th of this month, reading the newspaper and carrying the Beijing telegram, the Executive Yuan ordered the Ministry of Foreign Affairs that all Chinese and foreign merchants in the concessions of various countries should pay the business tax levied by our country in accordance with the regulations and must not resist. It can be seen that our central government has insight into power and justice, and upholds the utmost fairness. The various trade associations are willing to uphold the sincerity of patriotism and support the central government's negotiations to promote business tax. Shanghai has special circumstances and cannot be compared with other provinces and cities. Before this negotiation is settled, our wise municipal authorities should not bear to impose partial taxation on our Chinese community and our Chinese merchants alone. This is a declaration, I hope you will understand."

Zhang Qun Talks About Wharf Dues

The Municipal Government is Negotiating with the Jianghai Customs

It Can Be Implemented Next Month

Regarding the recovery of wharf dues, the municipal government has completed negotiations with the authorities of the Public Concession and the French Concession. Wharf dues have been collected by the Jianghai Customs on behalf of the government, amounting to more than 1 million yuan per year, all of which are handed over to the Public Concession and the French Concession Bureau. The municipal government only receives 10,000 yuan per year. Now, the municipal government has agreed with the British and French concessions on the recovery method. All wharf dues are still collected by the Jianghai Customs on behalf of the government. As for the distribution method, those belonging to the Public Concession and the French Concession, the dues will be handed over to the two Concession Bureaus. Those belonging to the Chinese territory, such as the wharf dues of Nanshi, Pudong, and Jiangxin, will be completely allocated to the municipal government. In this way, the municipal government can increase its revenue by more than 700,000 yuan per year. Our reporter especially met with Mayor Zhang Qun yesterday. According to reports, regarding the issue of recovering wharf dues, the municipal government has signed a contract with the two Concession Bureaus, and is now directly negotiating with the Jianghai Customs on future collection procedures. It is rumored that the Ministry of Finance will issue a transfer order, which is not true. It is expected that a complete agreement can be reached in these few days, and it is hoped that it can be implemented starting from May. Furthermore, because Mr. Zhang was newly appointed as the director of the National Assembly Reception, he took the 11:45 pm night train to Beijing last night to negotiate everything and is scheduled to return to Shanghai on the 25th.

Trade Associations

Article 10 of the Detailed Rules for the Trade Association Law

Telegram from the National Federation of Commerce

Requesting Expression of Opinions from All Parties

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce yesterday sent a telegram to all chambers of commerce nationwide, stating: "It has been found that the Ministry of Industry has revised Article 10 of the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Trade Association Law, which reads: 'Article 10: Members under Article 7 of this Law, each company or firm may send one or two representatives, limited to managers or principals. If the average number of shop employees exceeds ten in the most recent year, one additional representative should be sent, to be elected by the shop employees of the respective company or firm, but not exceeding three representatives in total.' This Federation believes that the amendment of this article poses a significant impediment to the fundamental organization of trade associations and chambers of commerce. On March 7th, we submitted a telegram in lieu of a formal report to the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, and the Ministry of Industry, requesting its correction. The telegram stated: 'We have found that Article 10 of the revised Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Trade Association Law stipulates that members' representatives under Article 7 of this Law, each company or firm may send one or two representatives, limited to managers or principals. However, if the average number of employees used in the most recent year is fifteen or more, one additional representative may be sent, to be elected by the employees of the respective company or firm.' Recently, the latter half of this article has been amended to: 'However, if the average number of employees used in the most recent year exceeds ten, one additional representative may be sent, to be elected by the employees of the respective company or firm, but not exceeding three representatives in total.' It has been found that in commercial ports and metropolitan areas, companies and firms with thirty or more employees account for over sixty percent. According to this article, the managers and principals who are trade association member representatives would only account for two-fifths, while the employees would account for three-fifths. During discussions and voting, employees would inevitably hold an absolute majority. Shop owners and shop employees have different positions, and disputes are bound to arise. This would nominally be a trade association but would effectively be an employee association, which is likely not the original intent of the state in creating the Trade Association Law. We earnestly request that the Ministry of Industry be instructed to amend the article back to: 'Each company or firm should send one or two member representatives, limited to managers or principals. If the average number of employees used in the most recent year is fifteen or more, one additional member representative may be sent, to be elected by the employees.' This would prevent the reversal of roles between owners and employees and ensure the prosperity of both industry and commerce, which is our sincere plea.'" After the submission, on April 2nd, the Executive Yuan issued Decree No. 114, stating: "The telegram in lieu of a formal report is noted. This case has been referred to the Ministry of Industry for review. According to their response, the amendment of the article was initiated by the Central Training Department, based on four excerpts of summaries prepared by the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters on the reorganization of trade unions in the city, requesting the enactment of regulations for the organization of shop employees. It was deemed relevant to the aforementioned laws and regulations, and the Ministry was requested to send representatives to a meeting. It was resolved to amend Article 10 of the Detailed Rules for Implementation to provide more opportunities for shop employees to participate in group organizations. In addition to being promulgated and circulated by the Ministry, it has also been submitted to the Yuan for onward submission to the National Government for record. The request for amendment cannot be approved." Based on this, it is found that the deliberations are generally appropriate and should be approved accordingly. Aside from issuing instructions, this decree is issued for notification. According to the revised articles of the Ministry of Industry, company and firm representatives attending trade associations, managers, and principals would only number two, while employees would number three, representing a ratio of two-fifths to three-fifths. By this analogy, employees will inevitably constitute an absolute majority in trade associations, while managers and principals will constitute a minority. Regardless of proposals or voting, the rights of employees will inevitably outweigh those of managers and principals. Nominally, this would be a trade association, but in reality, it would be an association of factory workers and shop employees. This not only contradicts the original legislative intent of the Trade Association Law but also differs in nature. With differing interests, conflicts will inevitably occur from time to time, and disputes will inevitably arise, which is one concern. Chambers of commerce are based on trade associations, and trade associations elect representatives to participate in chambers of commerce. As member representatives, they will invariably be factory workers and shop employees who are elected. Assembling factory workers and shop employees from various trade associations to form a chamber of commerce would effectively make the chamber of commerce a general assembly of factory workers and shop employees. Not only would the chamber of commerce exist in name only, contradicting the original legislative intent of the Chamber of Commerce Law, but there is also the concern that a

Page 14

region's own businesses would lack a body for collective deliberation and expression of views. The thirty-plus year history of chambers of commerce would inevitably come to an end, which would be unfortunate not only for the business community but also for the government. This is another concern. The two aforementioned points relate to the fundamental organization of the Trade Association Law and the Chamber of Commerce Law and represent a matter of life and death for the business community nationwide. It seems imperative to make a thorough effort to strive for amendment in order to achieve the goal of revision. This is a corresponding telegram for your information. It is hoped that you will promptly express your opinions and telegram the Central Government to appeal for approval of the amendment. The situation is urgent, and we earnestly hope for its implementation. Respectfully submitted by Lin Kanghou, Chairman; Su Minsheng, Zhang Yuquan, Lu Guangxu, Chen Riping, Li Kuian, Peng Chuli, and others of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of the Republic of China.

Records of Contemporary Figures' Movements

Hong Kong Government Certifies White Case as Baseless

Bai Zhiying Trafficking Drugs is a Rumor

Hong Kong Customs Responsible for Certification

Huang Jiaohui, Director-General of the China National Anti-Narcotics Association, previously traveled to Taiwan with his wife, Dr. Bai Zhiying, to inspect the opium prohibition situation. Suddenly, rumors were fabricated, claiming that Huang's wife was trafficking morphine and was apprehended by Hong Kong Customs, which was publicized both domestically and internationally. After Huang and his wife returned from overseas, they repeatedly declared the claims to be false. The Anti-Narcotics Association and the Party Headquarters also issued statements on their behalf, confirming that they were falsely accused, and the truth has gradually become clear. It is reported that at the beginning of the month, Huang and his wife entrusted Mr. Pender Hake, barrister at the Gu Tai Public Law Office, and Messrs. Wilkinson and Grist, barristers in Hong Kong, to investigate with the Hong Kong government and obtain a certificate from Hong Kong Customs, proving that the matter of Mrs. Huang trafficking drugs was entirely untrue. The translation of the certificate from Mr. J.D. Lloyd, Superintendent of Imports and Exports of Hong Kong Customs, No. 189, dated April 15, to Messrs. Wilkinson and Grist, barristers in Hong Kong, is as follows: "We acknowledge receipt of your letter inquiring whether there is any basis for rumors regarding Dr. Bai Zhiying trafficking morphine. We hereby reply as follows: Hong Kong Customs has not recently apprehended any case of smuggling morphine involving a Chinese woman. Furthermore, a review of reports from past years, such as 1927, 1928, 1929, up to the present, shows no such cases involving Chinese women. This is hereby certified." Furthermore, the investigation report from Messrs. Wilkinson and Grist, barristers in Hong Kong, to Mr. Hake, barrister at the Guwo Public Law Office, is excerpted as follows: "We were entrusted to visit and inquire with the Chinese Customs Tax Commissioner in Hong Kong regarding the rumors of Mrs. Huang trafficking drugs. According to the Tax Commissioner, I also received a request from a supervisor of a certain Chinese Customs to investigate this case, but the investigation revealed no evidence of Dr. Bai Zhiying smuggling morphine. Our lawyers immediately visited and inquired with the Superintendent of Imports and Exports of Hong Kong Customs, who stated that the Customs had no evidence of Bai Zhiying trafficking drugs. In fact, since 1927, this Customs has not apprehended any case of smuggling narcotics involving a Chinese woman. We are enclosing the certificate from Mr. Lloyd, the Customs Superintendent." It is reported that the Anti-Narcotics Association is preparing to make a large-scale exoneration for Mr. and Mrs. Huang. Mr. and Mrs. Huang are also planning to invite domestic and foreign journalists in the coming days to announce the truth of the false accusations.
